Add the [[Parsley|parsley]], [[Coriander|coriander]] and [[Mint|mint]] and mix it in thoroughly by [[Hand|hand]].\n| Form the paste into [[Sausages|sausages]] and press metal [[skewers]] along their length, tamping the [[Meat|meat]] around the skewer. Alternatively, form the [[Meat|meat]] into small [[Meatballs|meatballs]]. \n| [[Brush]] with a little [[Oil|oil]] and [[Grill|grill]] for 6 to 8 minutes, turning once or twice.\n}}\n(''Jill Dupleix in The Times T2'')\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Moroccan kebab sticks ready to grill.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Moroccan kebab sticks ready to grill\nImage:Mince from lamb fillet.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Roughly slice the [[lamb fillet]] and then blitz in a [[food processor]] with a metal blade\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with the [[Yoghurt|yogurt]], scattered with [[Paprika|paprika]], some [[Lemon wedges|lemon wedges]] and a [[Green salad|green salad]].\n===Variations===\nCook this on a barbecue.\n===Chef's notes===\nNicer mince: Buy lamb fillet and run it through a [[meat mincer]] or if you don't have one, blitz for 10 seconds in a [[food processor]] with a metal blade.\n\nFor 2 people, I used 1 small lamb fillet , 1 small onion and kept the remaining ingredients the same.\n\nFor a nice simple, spicy kebab, just roll the kebab in [[Taste Sensation Fiery Moroccan marinade favouring]] before grilling.\n\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/rose-harissa.html Belazu Rose Harissa]\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#moroccankebabsticks #foodprocessor #coriander #mint #parsley #paprika #onion #yoghurt #lamb #unusualrecipes #harissa </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] \n| 165g [[Red lentils|red lentils]] \n| 1.5 [[Litres|litres]] of [[chicken stock]] \n| [[Juice|juice]] &frac12; [[Lemon|lemon]] \n| 1 x 20g pack fresh [[Coriander|coriander]], chopped\n| 1.5 tablespoons extra [[Belazu]] [[Argan Oil]] to serve \n| [[Salt|salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] to season\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] and [[Butter|butter]] in a large heavy-based pan\n| Add the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Carrots|carrots]], cover and cook over a low heat until beginning to soften.\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and cook for a minute, add the [[Spices|spices]], stir and cook for a further minute.\n| Add the [[Lentils|lentils]], stir, then add the [[Stock|stock]], bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]], partially covered, for 25-30 minutes, until the lentils are soft.\n| Cool a little, then liquidise and return to the pan. Season the [[Soup|soup]], add the [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] to taste and gently reheat.\n| Stir in the fresh [[Coriander|coriander]], reserving a little for the garnish. \n| Drizzle the [[Argan Oil]] over the [[Soup|soup]] before serving.\n}}\n===Variations===\n[[Mint]] is often used as a garnish with Moroccan dishes\n(''Sainsbury's Magazine'')\n\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/argan-oil.html Belazu Argan Oil]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#arganoil #moroccanredlentilsoupwithcoriander #soup #garlic #coriander #carrots #belazu #butter #onions #lemon #spices </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Philadelphia spiced lamb",
                "revisions": [
                    {

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Philadelphia spiced lamb a cheese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#philadelphiaspicedlamb #garammasala #garlic #lamb #ginger #groundalmonds #onions #blackpepper #greensalad #sauce #groundcoriander \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A really simple way to make a quick, spicy, creamy North African-style meal\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4176\n|PortionCalories = 1044\n|DatePublished=26th April 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  40 minutes\n|PrepTime =  5 minutes\n|CookTime =  35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Philadelphia spiced lamb recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Eazy curry</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.9</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Not a bad curry, quick too.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nA really simple way to make a quick, spicy, creamy [[North African]]-style meal.\n\n{{PhiladelphiaPermission}}\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 kg [[Lamb|lamb]] pieces (tenderloin fillet if possible)\n| 120 g [[Philadelphia Original]]\n| 100 g [[Ground almonds|ground almonds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Garam masala|garam masala]]\n| 4 cm piece of [[Ginger|ginger]] peeled & chopped\n| 2 [[Cloves|cloves]] [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]] sliced\n| 1 tablespoon [[Oil|oil]]\n}}\n'''to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| serve with [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]] and a [[Green salad|green salad]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Place the Philly, [[Almonds|almonds]], [[Ginger|ginger]] and, [[Garlic|garlic]] into a [[Blender|blender]] with 200ml water and [[Blend|blend]] until smooth then stir in the [[Garam masala|garam masala]].\n| Heat a large pan and add the [[Oil|oil]], [[Brown|brown]] the [[Meat|meat]] on all sides then remove from the pan.\n| Lower the heat, tip in the [[Onions|onions]] and cook until they are soft and [[Brown|brown]].\n| Return the [[Meat|meat]] to the pan and pour over the [[Sauce|sauce]].\n| Bring to a [[Simmer|simmer]] and put a lid on the pan.\n| Cook for 30 mins until the [[Lamb|lamb]] is cooked and tender.\n}}\n\n===Variations===\nIf you don't have [[Garam masala|garam masala]], use a mixture of [[Chilli title": "Pitta bread recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pitta bread, a breadmaker recipe Cooking Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#wholemealflour #yeast #dough #breadmaker #warmplace #vitaminc #pittabreadrecipe #yellowcornmeal #flour #whiteflour #bakingtray \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Pita (pita bread, pitta or pitta bread) is a wheat flatbread made with yeast. It can be white (normal flour) or brown when made with wholemeal flour\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{recipesummary\n|Image comment = The best pitta breads you will ever have tasted\n|Servings = 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 1 hour\n|DatePublished=25th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|PrepTime = 45 minutes\n|CookTime = 15 minutes\n|TotalCalories = 1035\n|PortionCalories = 258\n|Image = [[Image:Pitta bread ready to eat.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nicer than shop bought pittas</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">These have a lovely chwy texture that you don't get from commercial pittas.  The outsides are always crunchy too.  Lovely</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Pitta bread arms length.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Roll them out the length of your arm!]]\nPita (pita bread, pitta or pitta bread) is a [[wheat]] flatbread made with [[yeast]]. It can be white (normal flour) or brown when made with [[wholemeal flour]]. \n\nSimilar to other double-layered flat or pocket breads, pita is traditional in many Middle Eastern and Mediterranean cuisines. It is prevalent from North Africa and the Middle East.\n\nThe Indian flatbread form of [[roti]] is sometimes referred to as \"Indian pita\".\n\nWe also have a [[Crispbread|brilliantly simple recipe]] that in a few moments turns normal pitta breads into buttery crispbread. You won't believe how good it is until you try it.\n\nThis recipe is simple and delicious and the results are far better than shop-bought pittas.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| &#190; a teaspoon of [[Dried active yeast|dried active yeast]]\n| 250 g (8.5 oz) strong white flour\n| &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; or 200 g (7 oz) strong [[white flour]] and 50 g (1.5 oz) strong [[Wholemeal flour|wholemeal flour]] for a light wholemeal pitta\n| A pinch of [[ascorbic acid]] or 1 [[vitamin C]] tablet, crushed between 2 tablespoons - (''300mg to 500 mg'') - ''optional''\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 145 ml water\n\n}}\n===Method===\n\n\n'''Hand method'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix a little of the water (which should be at body temperature/lukewarm, about 37\u00b0C) with the [[Sugar|sugar]] and the [[Yeast|yeast]], whisk up and leave in a [[warm place]] for 10 minutes to froth up\n| Mix the [[Yeast|yeast]] solution together with the remaining ingredients and [[Kneading bread|knead]] for 10 minutes until you have a pliable [[dough]]\n| Cover with a damp [[Tea|tea]] towel and leave in a [[warm place]] for about an hour to rise\n}}\n\n'''Breadmaker method'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Tip all of the ingredients into your [[bread maker]]\n| Set it to the short [[dough]] program (normally the pizza dough setting)\n| Panasonic SD253 breadmaker, use pizza setting.\n| '''[[Panasonic SD-ZB2502 automatic breadmaker]] use menu option 22, pizza dough setting.'''\n| 45 minutes later, proceed as below\n}}\n\n'''Either method - continue from here'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Divide into 4 balls [about 100g each] and roll out into oval shapes, about the length of your arm.\n| If you have the time, leave in a [[warm place]] for 30 minutes to rise a little\n| Preheat the [[grill]]\n| Place on a [[Yellow cornmeal|cornmeal dusted]] [[pizza stone]] or lightly oiled [[baking tray]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 5 to 6 minutes, keeping a watchful eye on them.\n}}\n===Chef's tip===\n\nDon't allow these to get too [[Browned|browned]], especially if you are likely to reheat them again before eating.\n\nWe made the batch shown with [[wholemeal flour]] (plus 1/4 of a crushed [[vitamin C]] tablet, for the ascorbic acid needed when using [[wholemeal flour]] in a [[bread maker]])\n\nIf the [[dough]] is a little too wet (or dry), just add a little more [[flour]] (or water) and run it through the [[bread maker]] again. It only takes another 45 minutes and no further involvement on your part.\n\nAlthough this recipe quantity ideally makes 4 pitta breads, you can make 6 mini pittas instead.  They are smaller than pittas we find in the UK, but are great for little snack pockets if filled!\n\n===Arm's length roll out===\nAfter reading The Fabulous Baker Brothers cookbook [ISBN 0755363701, 9780755363704] and following their suggestion to roll the pittas ''the length of your forearm'', that's what I now do.  The pittas generally shrink when they puff up so you get lovely oval pittas.  Thanks guys!\n\n===Variations===\n\nSee the [[Talk:Pitta bread recipe|comments page]] page for variations to this recipe. \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Breadmaker recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Prepared foods]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#wholemealflour #yeast #dough #breadmaker #warmplace #vitaminc #pittabreadrecipe #yellowcornmeal #flour #whiteflour #bakingtray </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

title": "Rice with spices, re-fried lamb, allspice and sweet onions, served with a cooling yoghurt sauce",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Rice with spices, re-fried lamb, allspice and sweet onions recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#yoghurt #rice #lamb #onions #sauce #cucumber #coriander #almonds #fridge #roast #groundcoriander \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=There is no nicer or simpler way to revive lamb leftover from a roast and spare boiled rice than to put it in a pan with onions that have been cooked\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1256\n|PortionCalories = 314\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Rice with spices, re-fried lamb, allspice and sweet onions, served with a cooling yoghurt sauce recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Complex title!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Simple recipe though!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nThere is no nicer or simpler way to revive [[Lamb|lamb]] leftover from a [[Roast|roast]] and spare [[Boiled rice|boiled rice]]* than to put it in a pan with [[Onions|onions]] that have been cooked until sweet and add the comforting fragrance of [[Allspice|allspice]] and [[Coriander|coriander]]. \n\nThis is an economical dish all the family will love, served with a cooling [[Yoghurt|yogurt]], coriander and [[Cucumber|cucumber]] [[Sauce|sauce]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 tablespoons [[Butter|butter]], [[Dripping|dripping]] or [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]]\n| 4 medium white [[Onions|onions]], peeled and chopped\n| 8 tablespoons leftover [[Roasted|roasted]] [[Lamb|lamb]], cut into slithers\n| 2 teaspoons [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground allspice|ground allspice]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]]\n| 2 tablespoons flaked [[Almonds|almonds]]\n}}\n'''For the [[Yoghurt|yogurt]] [[Sauce|sauce]]:'''\n* 6 tablespoons whole [[Milk|milk]] natural [[Yoghurt|yogurt]] or [[Greek yogurt]]\n* 4 sprigs [[Coriander|coriander]], chopped\n* &frac14; [[Cucumber|cucumber]], halved lengthways, deseeded and then chopped\n* 2 teaspoons [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]] (optional)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| First make the [[Sauce|sauce]], combining the [[Yoghurt|yogurt]] with the [[Coriander|coriander]] and [[Cucumber|cucumber]] in a bowl.\n| Heat the [[Fat|fat]] in a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] over a medium-low heat and add the [[Onions|onions]]. \n| Cook slowly for about 10-15 minutes until they are a pale gold colour.\n| Add the [[Lamb|lamb]] with the [[Spice|spice]] and [[Fry|fry]] for 2 minutes, stirring often. Then add the [[Rice|rice]] and cook turning it with a spatula to make sure it is well heated. \n| Taste and add [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] if necessary. \n| Transfer to a serving dish.\n| In a small pan, toast the [[Almonds|almonds]] until golden then scatter over the [[Rice|rice]]. \n| Serve the [[Rice|rice]] with the [[Yoghurt|yogurt]] on the side.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\n* Leftover [[Rice|rice]] is safe to use if it has been stored in the [[Fridge|fridge]] soon after cooking, and is reheated fully. \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:British Onions recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n{{Template:British Onions attribution}}\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#yoghurt #rice #lamb #onions #sauce #cucumber #coriander #almonds #fridge #roast #groundcoriander </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Roast leg of lamb (Moroccan-style) a meat recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#roastpotatoes #marinade #legoflamb #butter #harissapaste #ghee #roast #marinate #parsley #cuminseeds #roasted \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=By far the most popular meat of Morocco, this leg of lamb is an oven-roasted version of Mechoui\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4867\n|PortionCalories = 811\n|DatePublished=10th March 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 14 hours 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 12 hours 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Roast leg of lamb (Moroccan-style) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Lamb at its best</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">The more garlic, the better</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nBy far the most popular [[Meat|meat]] of Morocco, this [[Leg of lamb|leg of lamb]] is an [[Oven|oven]]-[[Roasted|roasted]] version of [[M\u00e9choui]].  You won't need to carve this, you should be able to serve by pulling the tender [[Meat|meat]] away from the bone with a fork.  Serve with [[Roast potatoes|roast potatoes]], a selection of vegetables and [[Harissa paste|harissa paste]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.5 kg (3.5 lb) [[Leg of lamb|leg of lamb]]\n}}\n'''[[Marinade|marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 40 g 1.5 oz [[Butter|butter]] or [[Ghee|ghee]]\n| 2 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed (or to taste)\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| &#188; teaspoons [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] (or to taste)\n| 1 teaspoon of fine [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n'''to garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Fresh [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] or [[Parsley|parsley]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n*Prepare the [[Meat|meat]] the day before so it can [[Marinate|marinate]] overnight\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Trim the [[Meat|meat]] of excess [[Fat|fat]]\n| Carefully stab the joint all over with a knife\n| Blend the [[Marinade|marinade]] ingredients to a paste.  Soften the [[butter]] or [[ghee]] by microwaving for 20 seconds to make the mixing easier. \n| Spread this all over the surface of the [[Lamb|lamb]], pushing it into all of the the cuts.\n| Place in a [[sealable container]] and leave overnight in a [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]] to [[Marinate|marinate]]\n}}\n'''the next day'''\n# Remove the [[Leg of lamb|leg of lamb]] from the container and place the a large [[roasting tray]].\n# Free any solidified butter by microwaving the container for 30 seconds.  Add this to the joint.\n# [[Roast|roast]] the joint at 220\u00b0 C for 15 minutes.  Don't be concerned by the burning [[Butter|butter]], it will add to the flavour.\n# Reduce the [[Oven|oven]] temperature to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4) and [[Roast|roast]] for a further 2 hours.  [[Baste]] regularly\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Roast leg of lamb (Moroccan-style) preserved lemons.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Buttery marinade (with preserved lemon flesh)\nImage:Roast leg of lamb (Moroccan-style) ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Simple ingredients - (I eventually cut many more slashes than is shown here)\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nAllow to rest for 10 minutes and serve with [[Roast potatoes|roast potatoes]],  [[Harissa paste|harissa paste]] and a selection of [[Vegetables|vegetables]].\n===Variations===\nChop/ squash half of a [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] and add it to the [[marinade]].\n===Chef's notes===\nDon't be put off a recipe that calls for a leg of lamb because of the high cost.  This recipe can be adjusted for [[Frozen lamb - what great value!|half a leg of lamb and you buy that (frozen)]] for just \u00a36.00! (March 2013).\n==See also==\n* [[Roast potatoes]]\n* [[Roast vegetables]]\n* [[Gravy recipes]]\n* [[Perfect Yorkshire puddings]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#roastpotatoes #marinade #legoflamb #butter #harissapaste #ghee #roast #marinate #parsley #cuminseeds #roasted </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Shakshouka",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Shakshouka, Egg recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tomatoes #shakshouka #eggs #garlic #onions #oliveoil #peppers #pita #onion #eggyolks #paprikapowder \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Shakshouka (shakshoka, chakchouka, shak-shouka, shak shouka) is a Tunisian and Israeli dish made of cooked tomatoes, peppers, spices and eggs\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 524\n|PortionCalories = 131\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 40 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Shakshouka recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A slap-up meal, or what!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Fabulous.  I'm glad I made this - thank you!</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Shakshouka''' ('''shakshoka''', '''chakchouka''', '''shak-shouka''', '''shak shouka''') is a Tunisian and Israeli dish made of cooked [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Spices|spices]] and [[Eggs|eggs]]. It is very similar to the Turkish dish Menemen and to the Latin American breakfast dish [[Huevos Rancheros|huevos rancheros]].\n\nIn Israeli cuisine, the dish is made of [[Eggs|eggs]], [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], and [[Onions|onions]] or [[Garlic|garlic]]. Shakshouka is typically eaten with a [[Pita|pita]], like many other Middle Eastern dishes, or with white [[Bread|bread]] that is dipped in it.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 3 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 4 large [[Free range eggs|free range eggs]]\n| 1 small sweet [[Red pepper|red pepper]], deseeded and sliced finely\n| 6 medium [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 1 tablespoon sweet [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] until soft in about a tablespoons of [[Olive oil|olive oil]], flavoured with a grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]].  This will take about 8 minutes.\n| Meanwhile, grate the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] using the coarsest [[Grater|grater]] you have.\n| Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Paprika|paprika]] and mix well.\n| Season to taste\n| Cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] on a very low heat for 25 minutes.\n| After 25 minutes, break the [[Eggs|eggs]] on to the surface of the [[Tomato|tomato]] mixture.\n| Cover and cook for 4 minutes or until the [[Eggs|eggs]] are done to your liking.\n}}\n===Variations===\nSome cooks like to break the [[Egg yolks|egg yolks]] and swirl them into the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tomatoes #shakshouka #eggs #garlic #onions #oliveoil #peppers #pita #onion #eggyolks #paprikapowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

title": "Skordalia",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Skordalia, Greek recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#skordalia #bread #garlic #oliveoil #vinegar #sauce #whitewinevinegar #eggs #cod #greekcuisine #dip \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Skordalia or skordhalia/skorthalia (\u03c3\u03ba\u03bf\u03c1\u03b4\u03b1\u03bb\u03b9\u03b1 skor\u00f0a'\u028ea; in Greek also called \u03b1\u03bb\u03b9\u03b1\u03b4\u03b1) is a thick puree (or sauce/dip/spread/etc.) in\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 132\n|PortionCalories = 33\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4 - Makes one jar of skordalia\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = None\n |Image = [[Image:Skordalia recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Tasty</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This was nice in a meze</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\nSkordalia or skordhalia/skorthalia (\u03c3\u03ba\u03bf\u03c1\u03b4\u03b1\u03bb\u03b9\u03ac [skor\u00f0a'\u028ea]; in Greek also called \u03b1\u03bb\u03b9\u03ac\u03b4\u03b1) is a thick [[Puree|puree]] (or [[Sauce|sauce]]/[[Dip|dip]]/spread/etc.) in [[Greek cuisine]] made by combining Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]] with a bulky base\u2014which may be a pur\u00e9e of [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Walnuts|walnuts]], [[Almonds|almonds]], or liquid-soaked stale [[Bread|bread]]\u2014and then beating in [[Olive oil|olive oil]] to make a smooth emulsion. [[Vinegar]] is often added. Variants may include [[Eggs|eggs]] as an emulsifier and omitting or reducing the bulk ingredient, which makes for a result similar to the Proven\u00e7al a\u00efoli, Catalan allioli, and so on. In the Ionian Islands [[Cod|cod]] [[Stock|stock]], and [[Lemon|lemon]] instead of vinegar is usually added, and Skordalia is eaten as a main dish.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 thick slice of tale white [[Bread|bread]], crusts removed\n| 4 large [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, peeled\n| 2 tablespoons [[White wine vinegar|white wine vinegar]]\n| 110 ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Soak the [[Bread|bread]] in water for 5 minutes then squeeze out most of the water\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Bread|bread]], [[Vinegar|vinegar]] to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a blade and pulse for a few seconds\n| Then leave the [[Blender|blender]] running and gently drizzle the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] into the processor until well blended\n| Taste and add [[Salt|salt]] if needed\n| If it's too thick, add a little water with a little more [[Oil|oil]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Meze|meze]], great with [[Grilled|grilled]] [[Fish|fish]] or [[Meat|meat]] and especially with [[Roasted|roasted]] [[Vegetables|vegetables]].\n===Variations===\nUse [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] instead of [[Vinegar|vinegar]]\nFor a [[Potato|potato]] based skordalia, peel 1 large potato, [[Boil|boil]] and [[Mash|mash]] and add in place of the [[Bread|bread]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Greek recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#skordalia #bread #garlic #oliveoil #vinegar #sauce #whitewinevinegar #eggs #cod #greekcuisine #dip </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

title": "Skordalia (V)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Skordalia vegetarian Greek sauce recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#bread #garlic #oliveoil #vinegar #skordaliav #potato #roasted #eggs #almonds #boil #cod \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Skordalia or skordhalia/skorthalia is a thick puree (or sauce/dip/spread/etc.)\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 132\n|PortionCalories = 33\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4 - Makes one jar of skordalia\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = None\n |Image = [[Image:Skordalia recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Lovely in a meze</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Nicer than hummus</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nSkordalia or skordhalia/skorthalia (\u03c3\u03ba\u03bf\u03c1\u03b4\u03b1\u03bb\u03b9\u03ac [skor\u00f0a'\u028ea]; in Greek also called \u03b1\u03bb\u03b9\u03ac\u03b4\u03b1) is a thick [[Puree|puree]] (or [[Sauce|sauce]]/[[Dip|dip]]/spread/etc.) in [[Greek cuisine]] made by combining Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]] with a bulky base\u2014which may be a pur\u00e9e of [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Walnuts|walnuts]], [[Almonds|almonds]], or liquid-soaked stale [[Bread|bread]]\u2014and then beating in [[Olive oil|olive oil]] to make a smooth emulsion. [[Vinegar]] is often added. Variants may include [[Eggs|eggs]] as an emulsifier and omitting or reducing the bulk ingredient, which makes for a result similar to the Proven\u00e7al a\u00efoli, Catalan allioli, and so on. In the Ionian Islands [[Cod|cod]] [[Stock|stock]], and [[Lemon|lemon]] instead of vinegar is usually added, and Skordalia is eaten as a main dish.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 thick slice of tale white [[Bread|bread]], crusts removed\n| 4 large [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, peeled\n| 2 tablespoons [[White wine vinegar|white wine vinegar]]\n| 110 ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Soak the [[Bread|bread]] in water for 5 minutes then squeeze out most of the water\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Bread|bread]], [[Vinegar|vinegar]] to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a blade and pulse for a few seconds\n| Then leave the [[Blender|blender]] running and gently drizzle the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] into the processor until well blended\n| Taste and add [[Salt|salt]] if needed\n| If it's too thick, add a little water with a little more [[Oil|oil]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Meze|meze]] or [[Roasted|roasted]] [[Vegetables|vegetables]].\n===Variations===\nUse [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] instead of [[Vinegar|vinegar]]\nFor a [[Potato|potato]] based skordalia, peel 1 large potato, [[Boil|boil]] and [[Mash|mash]] and add in place of the [[Bread|bread]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Greek recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#bread #garlic #oliveoil #vinegar #skordaliav #potato #roasted #eggs #almonds #boil #cod </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

It produces a far superior result to barbecuing, but does take a little longer.\n\nMade with a defrosted frozen half-leg of lamb, this lasted 2 people for 2 days - I used the same [[marinade]] ingredients as for 6 people, but with slightly less [[harissa paste]]. \n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tablespoon of [[coriander seeds]] \n| 1 tablespoon of [[cumin seeds]] \n| 3 tablespoons of Belazu Rose [[Harissa]] - I used 2 tablespoons of homemade [[Orange biter (hot chili sauce)]]\n| juice of 1 [[lemon]] \n| Belazu [[extra virgin olive oil]] \n| 3 cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]] \n| 1.6kg leg of [[lamb]], boned and butterflied (ask your butcher to do this for you)\n| I used a frozen half-leg of lamb and [[butterflied]] it myself.  It was a bit of a fiddle but it worked out fine in the end! \n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to its highest setting; 250\u00b0 C\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Marinaded half-leg of lamb cooked.jpg|After 3 hours in the oven\nImage:Marinaded half-leg of lamb.jpg|Marinaded, ready to cook\nImage:Butterflied half-leg of lamb.jpg|A poorly butterflied leg of lamb\nImage:Half-leg of lamb.jpg|Half-leg of (frozen) lamb, defrosted<br />[\u00a36.50 Morrisons - August 2013]\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Seeds|seeds]] in a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] and crush slightly. \n| Mix the [[Harissa]], [[Lemon|lemon]], 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Spices|spices]] together, smear over the [[Lamb|lamb]]\n| [[Marinate|marinate]] for at least three hours. \n| Place on an uncovered grill-tray at the top of the oven on its highest setting.\n| Cook for 15 minutes\n| Reduce the heat to 180\u00b0C [350\u00b0F - Gas 4], place the meat in an oven tray and cover with [[tin-foil]]\n| Cook for 2 hours 30 minutes - check now and then to ensure it is not drying out - reduce the heat if it is.\n| Allow to rest for 10 minutes before carving.\n}}\n(''[[Olive]] magazine'')\n\n===Serving suggestion===\nServe in [[homemade pitta breads]] with a selection of chopped salad vegetables.\n\n===See also===\n* [[Slow-roast recipes]]\n* [[Barbecued Harissa lamb]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mutton recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lamb #harissa #garlic #slowcookedlegoflambwithharissa #lemon #barbecuedharissalamb #oliveoil #spices #cuminseeds #butterflied #marinate </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

pepper]]\n| 3 tablespoons of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Halve the [[leeks]] and run them under a cold tap to wash out any mud\n| Lay the [[Leeks|leeks]], [[Rosemary|rosemary]], [[Thyme|thyme]] in the base of the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] and add half a [[Cup|cup]] of water\n| Halve the [[Tangerine|tangerine]] and place in the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] for the [[Lamb|lamb]] to sit on\n| Mix the rub ingredients together in a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]]\n| Stab and cut deep slashes in the [[Lamb|lamb]] leg and fill with the rub\n| Rub the remained over the surface of the [[Lamb|lamb]]\n| Place the [[Lamb|lamb]] on top of the bed of [[Leeks|leeks]]\n| Slow cook on low for about 5 hours\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px 100\u00b0C [225\u00b0F] so if you don't have a slow cooker you could use a [[casserole dish]] in an [[oven]] set to 100\u00b0 C (225\u00b0 F - gas \u00bc), [fan oven 80\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time We used [[Soya beans|soya beans]] because someone picked up the wrong cans.  It was just as good as normal!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 4 to 6 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]] ''or to taste''\n| 2 teaspoons [[turmeric powder]]\n| 2 teaspoons of (white) [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| &#189; of a teaspoon of [[Ground cinnamon|ground cinnamon]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] ''or to taste''\n| &#189; of a teaspoon of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon runny [[Honey|honey]] (normal honey heated in a [[Microwave|microwave]] for 10 seconds will be runny honey)\n| 3 medium [[Carrots|carrots]], peeled and sliced diagonally\n| 2 x 400g cans of [[Chick-peas|chick-peas]], well rinsed and drained\n}}\n''' to garnish'''\n* Bunch of [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], chopped\n* [[Lemon wedges]]\n* 150ml natural [[Yoghurt|yogurt]]\n* 4 slices of crusty [[Bread|bread]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Tagine|tagine]] or pan\n| Gently saut\u00e9 the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] for 6 minutes or until soft and translucent\n| Add the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], [[Turmeric|turmeric]], [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Honey|honey]], [[Black pepper|black pepper]] and the [[Carrots|carrots]]\n| Add enough water to almost cover the [[Carrots|carrots]] - not too much, you don't want [[Soup|soup]]!\n| Cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 15 minutes\n| Add the [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] and a little more water if the pan is [[Drying|drying]] out and heat for a further 5 to 10 minutes until the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] are cooked to your liking.\n}}\n==See also==\n{{Tagine-recipe-list}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Algerian recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Libyan recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#carrots #cuminseeds #spicycarrotandchickpeatagine #tagine #onion #garlic #honey #microwave #chickpeas #turmeric #vegetarian </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Yum!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 120 g (4.5 oz) [[Dried|dried]] [[Chick peas|chick peas]] (60 g per person)\n| 2 teaspoons [[Caraway seeds|caraway seeds]], bruised in a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Black cumin seeds|black cumin seeds]], bruised in a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], chopped\n| 4 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Soak the [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] in cold water for at least 24 hours, rinsing now and then\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Drain the soaked [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]]\n| Add to a large pas of un[[Salt|salt]]ed [[Boiling|boiling]] water. Add any salt after the cooking process otherwise the [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] (or any [[Pulses|pulses]]) will harden.\n| [[Boil]] for about 1 hour.  Test a few to check they are done. The longer they soak for, the less cooking time they will need).\n| Drain and allow to cool.  Reserve a little liquid in case you need to 'soften' the mixture.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Spices|spices]] until they pop.\n| Add the chopped onions and fry for 6 minutes.\n| Add the cooked [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] stir and remove from the heat.\n| Add the contents to a [[Food processor|food processor]] and blitz to your desired consistency.\n| Add [[Salt|salt]] to taste. Add a little of the cooking water if the mixture is too dry.\n}}\n===Variations===\nSubstitute just about any spices to this so it suits your taste.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chickpeas #spicychickpeas #pestleandmortar #dried #boil #carawayseeds #pulses #blackcuminseeds #chickpea #panfried #fry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Add any salt after the cooking process otherwise the [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] (or any [[Pulses|pulses]]) will harden.\n| [[Boil]] for about an hour.  Test a few to check they are done. The longer they soak for, the less cooking time they will need).\n| Drain and allow to cool.  Reserve a little liquid in case you need to 'soften' the mixture.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Spices|spices]] until they pop.\n| Add the chopped onions and fry for 6 minutes.\n| Add the cooked [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] stir and remove from the heat.\n| Add the contents to a [[Food processor|food processor]] and blitz to your desired consistency.\n| Add [[Salt|salt]] to taste. Add a little of the cooking water if the mixture is too dry.\n}}\n===Variations===\nSustitute just about any spices to this so it suits your taste.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chickpeas #pestleandmortar #spices #boiling #dried #miseenplace #pulses #oliveoil #blackcuminseeds #spicychickpeasv #panfried </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Tip: ''Use normal [[Honey|honey]] and [[Microwave|microwave]] it for a few seconds.''\n| 3 [[Clove buds|clove buds]]\n| 1 [[Cinnamon stick]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Chilli flakes|chilli flakes]] or [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground ginger|ground ginger]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n'''to garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Freshly chopped [[Parsley|parsley]] or [[Coriander|coriander]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Pop the [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] pieces in a [[Steamer|steamer]] and [[Steam|steam]] for 10 minutes until the flesh is tender but not mushy.\n| Add the [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] and [[red onions]] to to an ovenproof dish that has been smeared with a little of the butter or ghee.\n| Melt the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a pan, add a good pinch of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] and once it starts to [[Bubble|bubble]], carefully stir in the remaining ingredients.\n| Pour the honey mixture over the squash and onions ensuring they are well coated.\n| [[Bake]] for 20 minutes in the middle of the [[Oven|oven]], turning once.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nPick out the [[Clove buds|clove buds]] and [[Cinnamon sticks|cinnamon sticks]] and serve garnished with [[Parsley|parsley]] or [[Coriander|coriander]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Algerian recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Libyan recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#ghee #parsley #clovebuds #butternutsquash #coriander #microwave #smen #speedpeeler #cinnamonstick #runnyhoney #chillipowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

However, the recipe does differ from one country to another.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 kg [[Courgettes|courgettes]]\n| 1 cup short [[Grain|grain]] [[Rice|rice]] (soaked in water for half an hour)\n| 200 g [[Lamb|lamb]] mice\n| 3 tablespoons [[Tomato paste|tomato paste]]\n| 4 [[Cloves of garlic|cloves of garlic]]\n| 1 tsp.  [[Salt|salt]]\n| &frac12; tsp. [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| &frac12; tsp. [[Cumin powder|cumin powder]]  \n| &frac14; tsp. [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Safflower|safflower]] \n| &frac14; teaspoon [[All spice|all spice]] \n| 1 teaspoon dry [[Mint|mint]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Rinse the [[Courgettes|courgettes]] and cut off the tops.\n| Core the [[Courgettes|courgettes]] with a [[Courgettes|courgettes]] corer. \n| In a large bowl, mix the [[Minced meat|minced meat]], [[Rice|rice]], [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]], [[Salt|salt]] and the [[Spices|spices]] until well combined. \n| To a large pot add [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]], water, and [[Salt|salt]] and bring to a [[Simmer|simmer]].\n|  Lightly work the [[Rice|rice]] [[Stuffing|stuffing]] into the [[Courgettes|courgettes]]. Ensure that each [[Courgette|courgette]] is only &frac34; full. This is too so that the rice need room to expand once cooked.\n|  To the [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]], add of the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Salt|salt]], and [[Dried|dried]] [[Mint|mint]] and stir. Slowly drop the [[Courgettes|courgettes]] into the [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]] and cover.\n|  Cook for about 35-45 minutes on medium heat.\n| Test the [[Courgettes|courgettes]] by tasting one and see if the [[Rice|rice]] is cooked and the [[Courgette|courgette]] is soft.\n|  Once cooked, take the [[Courgettes|courgettes]] out of the [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]] as they may break open if left too long in the [[Sauce|sauce]].\n}}\n===Variations===\nIn the same way, you can stuff [[Aubergine|aubergine]] and [[Peppers|peppers]].\n===Chef's notes===\nThis is the way stuffed [[Courgettes|courgettes]] is done in Damascus, it might differ from one city to another in Syria.\n==See also==\n\n* [[Courgette Corer]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Syrian recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mutton recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#courgettes #stuffedcourgette #rice #tomatosauce #mint #mincedmeat #vegetableoil #courgette #sauce #blackpepper #safflower </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Serve with simple [[Tomato salad|tomato salad]], a creamy-[[Garlic|garlic]] [[Hummus|hummus]], homemade [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]] and you will be in Casablanca - possibly.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]].\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]].\n| 1 medium whole [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Jointing a chicken|jointed, as shown here]], skin on.\n| 12 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], roughly chopped.\n| 2 tablespoons [[Sumac|sumac]] powder.\n| A pinch of [[oregano]].\n| 2 tablespoons [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]] or [[Red wine vinegar|red wine vinegar]].\n| Small pinch of [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], bruised in a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]].\n| 50 g [[Pine nuts|pine nuts]].\n| 3 tablespoons water.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Sumac baked chicken with pine-nuts recipe.jpg|Ready for the oven\nImage:Sumac in seed.jpg | Sumac 'fruit' cones remain on the tree for more than a year\nImage:Autumn sumac leaves.jpg | The Sumac tree has really pretty leaves in the Autumn\n</gallery>\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat 3 tablespoons of the [[Oil|oil]] a small [[Oven-proof casserole dish|oven proof casserole dish]] or [[Dutch oven]].\n| Season the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Brown|brown]] them, skin-side first, a few at a time and reserve.  Discard the [[Oil|oil]].\n| Lay the [[Onions|onions]] in the base of the pan and sprinkle with half of the [[Sumac|sumac]], the remaining tablespoons of [[Oil|oil]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]], 1 tablespoon of the [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]] and the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] and a pinch of [[oregano]].\n| Place the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces on top, skin-side up.  Sprinkle with the [[pine nuts]] and the remaining [[sumac]].\n| Heat the pan for a 3 or 4 minutes on the hob just to get it sizzling then place in the [[Oven|oven]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 35 minutes.\n| Place the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces on a preheated serving dish, [[Deglaze|deglaze]] the pan with the remaining tablespoons of [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]], add the water and mix well to produce a [[Sauce|sauce]].\n| Pour over the [[Chicken|chicken]] and serve immediately.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Hummus|hummus]], homemade [[Pitta bread|pitta bread]] and a simple [[Tomato salad|tomato salad]].\n===Variations===\nI added a whole [[onion]], roughly chopped, with the spring onions.\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #sumac #sherryvinegar #hummus #tomatosalad #sumacbakedchickenwithpinenuts #pinenuts #cuminseeds #oregano #bake #pittabread </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tabbouleh (Modern style) a vegetarian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#bulghurwheat #parsley #springonions #tomatoes #mint #lemonjuice #couscoustabbouleh #wheat #bulghur #flatleavedparsley #tabboulehsalad \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Originally large quantities of bulghur wheat was used and there were just small speckles of parsley\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 488\n|PortionCalories = 81\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 35 minutes\n |CookTime = 5 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Tabbouleh (Modern style) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Make sure you like parsley \ud83d\ude42</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">\u2026because you're in for a shock if you don't!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\nOriginally large quantities of [[Bulghur wheat|bulghur wheat]] was used and there were just small speckles of [[Parsley|parsley]].  This is a modern version, as nowadays, the weight of [[parsley]] can exceed the weight of [[Bulghur|bulghur]] [[Wheat|wheat]] by 5 to 1.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 50 g [[Bulghur wheat|bulghur wheat]]\n| 30 ml [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 8 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], finely chopped\n| 250 g [[Flat leaved parsley|flat leaved parsley]], finely chopped\n| 50 g [[Mint|mint]], finely chopped\n| 3 [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], skinned and roughly chopped\n| 75 ml Greek [[Olive oil|olive oil]] (I used [[Kalamata]])\n| Seasoning to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rinse the [[Bulghur wheat|bulghur wheat]], drain thoroughly and mix in the [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]].\n| Set aside for about 30 minutes.\n| Add the [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Parsley|parsley]], [[Mint|mint]] and [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], mix thoroughly.\n| Pour in the [[Oil|oil]] and seasoning, and mix (preferably with your hands).\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe on its own or use it to stuff [[Pitta breads|pitta bread]].  You can use crisp [[Lettuce|lettuce]] leaves to scoop it up, rather than a fork.\n===Variations===\nSee also [[Tabbouleh salad]] and [[Couscous tabbouleh]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Tabbouleh (modern style)]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Tabbouleh (modern style)]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Tabbouleh (modern style)]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Tabbouleh (modern style)]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes|Tabbouleh (modern style)]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Tabbouleh (modern style)]]\n[[Category:Starters|Tabbouleh (modern style)]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Tabbouleh (modern style)]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Tabbouleh (modern style)]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#bulghurwheat #parsley #springonions #tomatoes #mint #lemonjuice #couscoustabbouleh #wheat #bulghur #flatleavedparsley #tabboulehsalad </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Tabbouleh salad",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tabbouleh salad, Vegetarian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#parsley #springonions #lemonjuice #vegetables #lemon #tabboulehsalad #lime #fattoush #bulgurwheat #olives #bulgarwheat \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Tabbouleh, Syria's national dish, and very common in the Lebanon, is a Levantine dish, often used as part of a mezze\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1152\n|PortionCalories = 144\n|DatePublished=10th December 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 8\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 4 hours, 5 minutes\n|PrepTime = 4 hours\n|CookTime = 5 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Tabbouleh recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Very different to have this as a salad</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">But effective</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n\n'''Tabbouleh''', Syria's national dish, and very common in the Lebanon, is a Levantine dish, often used as part of a mezze. Its primary ingredients are bulgur, finely chopped [[parsley]], [[mint]], [[tomato]], [[spring onions]], and other [[herbs]] with [[lemon juice]], [[olive oil]] and various seasonings, generally including [[black pepper]] and sometimes [[cinnamon]] and [[allspice]]. It is similar to [[fattoush]], the main difference being [[fattoush]] is likely to contain fried [[pitta bread]] instead of [[bulgur wheat]] and the vegetables are roughly chopped.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 240ml [[bulgur wheat]]\n| 120ml [[olive oil]]\n| 120ml [[lemon juice]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt]]\n| [[Ground black pepper]] to taste\n| 1 [[cucumber]]\n| 1 bunch fresh [[parsley]]\n| &#189; [[green bell pepper]]\n| &#189; [[red bell pepper]]\n| 4 [[spring onions]]\n| Sliced ripe [[olives]] (optional)\n| 2-3 [[tomatoes]]\n| Thinly sliced [[lemon]] or [[lime]] to garnish\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cover the [[bulgar wheat]] in [[boiling]] water and let stand for five minutes, drain.\n| Add [[lemon juice]], [[oil]], [[salt]] and [[pepper]].\n| Stir, refrigerate while the rest of the [[vegetables]] are being chopped.\n| Peel, de-seed and finely chop the [[cucumbers]].\n| Core and finely chop the [[bell peppers]].\n| Remove the larger stems from the [[parsley]] and finely chop.\n| Finely chop the [[tomatoes]] and [[spring onions]]\n| Mix all [[vegetables]] along with [[olives]] and [[nutmeg]] into the [[bulgar wheat]].\n| Refrigerate at least four hours.\n| Sprinkle with chopped [[parsley]] and garnish with [[lemon]] or [[lime]] slices\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nCan be served as a [[main course]], or as an accompaniment or even as part of a meze\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Syrian recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#parsley #springonions #lemonjuice #vegetables #lemon #tabboulehsalad #lime #fattoush #bulgurwheat #olives #bulgarwheat </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Tabbouleh salad (Belazu)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tabbouleh salad (Belazu) a vegetarian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#parsley #springonions #lemonjuice #oliveoil #mint #greenolives #burghul #preservedlemon #tomatoes #tomato #belazu \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Tabbouleh, Syria's national dish, and very common in the Lebanon, is a Levantine dish\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 316\n|PortionCalories = 79\n|DatePublished=10th December 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Tabbouleh salad\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 1 hour 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 5 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Tabbouleh recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Not bad</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.7</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Not sure about the mint thouhg?</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Tabbouleh''', Syria's national dish, and very common in the Lebanon, is a Levantine dish, often used as part of a mezze. Its primary ingredients are bulgur, finely chopped [[parsley]], [[mint]], [[tomato]], [[spring onions]], and other [[herbs]] with [[lemon juice]], [[olive oil]] and various seasonings, generally including [[black pepper]] and sometimes [[cinnamon]] and [[allspice]]. It is similar to [[fattoush]], the main difference being [[fattoush]] is likely to contain fried [[pitta bread]] instead of [[bulgur wheat]] and the vegetables are roughly chopped.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 150g fine [[Burghul|burghul]] (or [[Barley|barley]] [[Couscous|couscous]]) \n| 2 [[Spring onions|spring onions]] \n| 2 [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] \n| 6 [[Belazu]] [[Green olives|green olives]] with [[Chilli|chilli]] \n| 1 [[Belazu]] [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] \n| 2 bunches [[Parsley|parsley]] \n| 1 bunch [[Mint|mint]] \n| 2 tablespoons extra virgin [[Olive oil|olive oil]] \n| 2 tablespoons [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] \n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]] \n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Cayenne pepper|cayenne pepper]] or [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rinse the [[Burghul|burghul]], then soak in cold water and cover for one hour until swollen.\n| Finely chop the [[Spring onions|spring onions]]. Cut the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] in half, squeeze out and discard the [[Seeds|seeds]] and [[Juice|juice]], and cut the remaining flesh into small [[Dice|dice]]. Finely chop the [[Green olives|green olives]]. Rinse the [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] (discard the flesh if salty) and finely slice the rind.\n| Pick off the [[Parsley|parsley]] and [[Mint leaves|mint leaves]], wash and dry them thoroughly, then roughly chop the leaves.\n| Drain the [[Burghul|burghul]] and squeeze dry. Toss with the [[Parsley|parsley]], [[Mint|mint]], [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Tomato|tomato]], [[Green olives|green olives]] and [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]]. Mix the [[Olive oil|olive oil]], [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Cayenne|cayenne]] and [[Sea Salt|sea salt]], and pour over the [[Salad|salad]]. Toss well, and serve.\n}}\n(''Jill Dupleix in The Times'')\n\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Syrian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n\n\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/belazu-pickled-lemons.html Belazu Preserved Lemon]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#parsley #springonions #lemonjuice #oliveoil #mint #greenolives #burghul #preservedlemon #tomatoes #tomato #belazu </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Yum!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nI like [[Tortilla Espa\u00f1ola|Tortilla espa\u00f1ola]] and I like [[Batatas harras]] (Lebanese [[Spiced potatoes|spiced potatoes]]), so decided to combine the two.  This is a [[Tortilla Espa\u00f1ola|Spanish omelette]] with [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Coriander|coriander]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 130 ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 kg [[Potatoes|potatoes]], preferably ones which are not floury, eg Cara, Nadine, peeled and sliced\n| 2 medium [[Onions|onions]], peeled and sliced\n| 2 bulbs [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and finely [[Diced|diced]]\n| 4 [[Chillies|chillies]], finely chopped\n| 70 g [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], finely chopped \n| 8 large [[Eggs|eggs]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a medium sized, deepish [[Frying pan|frying pan]] at a medium temperarure.\n| When hot, add the [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Chillies|chillies]].\n| Cover and reduce the heat, stirring from time to time until the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] are cooked and slightly [[Browned|browned]] (about 20 minutes).\n| Meanwhile, beat the [[Egg|egg]] and seasonings thoroughly in a bowl.\n| Drain off most of the excess [[Oil|oil]] and add the [[Potato|potato]] mixture to the [[Eggs|eggs]] and stir in the [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]].\n| Pour the whole lot back into the pan - there should be enough [[Oil|oil]] left to coat the bottom of the pan.\n| Increase the heat to medium again and cook the [[Omelette|omelette]] until the bottom and sides have set.\n| Turn out the [[Omelette|omelette]] onto a plate and slide it back into the pan upside down, so that the other side can be cooked. Alternatively, you can simply leave the omlette in the pan and place it under the [[Grill|grill]] until the top has set.\n| Once cooked, turn it out onto a plate and leave to cool. It is best served at room temperature.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Salad|salad]] or in a [[Baguette|baguette]].\n===Variations===\nUse as much or as little as you like of the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Coriander|coriander]].  Add other [[Spices|spices]] if you wish.\n\n{{OmeletteRecipes}}\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Tortilla 'batatas harras']]\n[[Category:Egg recipes|Tortilla 'batatas harras']]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Tortilla 'batatas harras']]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Tortilla 'batatas harras']]\n[[Category:Potato recipes|Tortilla 'batatas harras']]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Tortilla 'batatas harras']]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Tortilla 'batatas harras']]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Tortilla 'batatas harras']]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Tortilla 'batatas harras']]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tortillabatatasharras #chillies #garlic #potatoes #corianderleaves #onions #omelette #coriander #eggs #diced #egg </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Veal tongues with capers a beef recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tongue #sauce #vealtongueswithcapers #butter #veal #capers #simmer #vinegar #litres #boil #boiling \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe from my 1960's Lebanese cook book won't be to everyone's taste, however, if you're looking for an interesting way to cook veal tongue\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2377\n|PortionCalories = 594\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = As [[User:Robin|Robin]] says; \"Don't look at it too much, don't think about it too much!\"\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 3 hours\n |PrepTime = 30 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Veal tongues with capers recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Not for me!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is something I will not make.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe from my 1960's Lebanese cook book won't be to everyone's taste, however, if you're looking for an interesting way to cook [[Veal|veal]] [[Tongue|tongue]], this is probably it.\n\n[[Veal]] [[Tongue|tongue]] is more tender than [[Beef|beef]] tongue, but both require a good deal of cooking.  Speak to your butcher, you may be able to buy tongues prepared and ready cooked.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 medium tongues of [[Veal|veal]]\n| &#189; a [[Lemon|lemon]] and [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] for cleaning the [[Tongue|tongue]]\n| 2.5 tablespoons [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] (for [[Boiling|boiling]])\n| 200g (7 oz) [[White wine|white wine]]\n| 85g (3.5 oz) [[Carrots|carrots]], peeled and chopped\n| 85g (3.5 oz) [[Onions|onions]], peeled and sliced\n| 3.4 [[Litres|litres]] (6 [[Pints|pints]]) cold water for [[Boiling|boiling]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[White pepper|white pepper]]\n| 1 hot [[Chilli pepper|chilli pepper]], sliced into rings (de-seeded if desired)\n| 110g (4 oz) [[Butter|butter]]\n| 75g (3 oz) [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] (for the [[Sauce|sauce]])\n| 110g (4 oz) [[Capers|capers]] (rinsed and drained if [[Salted|salted]])\n| 25g (1 oz) [[Vinegar|vinegar]] (for [[Sauce|sauce]])\n}}\n===Method===\n\n'''cleaning the tongues'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Under cold running water, scrub the [[Tongue|tongues]] with a [[Brush|brush]].\n| Rub with half a [[Lemon|lemon]] and a handful of [[Salt|salt]] then leave for 15 minutes\n| Place the tongues in a large pan and cover with cold water\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 12 minutes, skimming any surface scum\n| Remove the tongues and discard the water and quickly rinse in cold water. Clean the pot\n}}\n'''cooking the tongues'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the tongues to the pot, together with 3.4 [[Litres|litres]] of cold water, the [[Vegetables|vegetables]], [[Wine|wine]], [[Herbs|herbs]] and 2.5 tablespoons of [[Salt|salt]]\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] until the tongues are cooked (about 2 to 2.5 hours)\n}}\n'''caper sauce'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Butter|butter]] and [[Flour|flour]], white pepper and salt to a small pan and once the [[Roux|roux]] browns, add enough of the [[Strained|strained]] [[Stock|stock]] to make the [[Sauce|sauce]]. Once it thickens, stir in the [[Chillies|chillies]].\n'''final preparation'''\n| Peel the tongues, removing any gristle, [[Fat|fat]] or connective tissues\n| Slice diagonally, a little less than 1 cm (&frac12;\")\n| Arrange on a large platter and sprinkle with half of the [[Capers|capers]]\n| Pour half of the [[Sauce|sauce]] over the tongues and [[Capers|capers]] and the rest, serve in a sauce dish.  Sprinkle the remaining capers over the final layer of sauce.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe this dish with [[Boiled potatoes|boiled potatoes]].\n===Chef's notes===\nThe [[Salt|salt]] and [[Butter|butter]] quantities are as in the original recipe, I would probably reduce them if you are at all health conscious.  The original recipe just specifies '[[Vinegar|vinegar]]' - Use your favourite, I dare to suggest [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]! \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Offal recipes]]\n[[Category:Veal recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tongue #sauce #vealtongueswithcapers #butter #veal #capers #simmer #vinegar #litres #boil #boiling </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->{{#seo:\n|title=Very fruity pumpkin curry (slow cooker recipe)\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#slowcooker #pumpkin #fry #blackpepper #pears #kiwifruit #banana #ghee #veryfruitypumpkincurryslowcookerrecipe #simmer #wok \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A great recipe for fulfilling your 5 a day portions.  It's vegetarian &amp; vegan and I have to say one of the best curries I've cooked in quite a while. Abel and Cole\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2392\n|PortionCalories = 598\n|DatePublished=27th April 2014\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 4 hours 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 4 hours\n |Image = [[Image: Very fruity pumpkin curry slow cooker recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Earthy food</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Great for a grey winter's day</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image: Very fruity pumpkin curry slow cooker.jpg|thumb|300px|right|After 4 hours]]\nThis is my very fruity variation of [[Pumpkin and chickpea curry]] which I've adapted for the [[slow cooker]].  We had the remnants of an [[Abel & Cole]] fruit and vegetable box to use up so this was ideal!  We'll be ok for our [[5 a day]] this weekend!\n\nThis Is a great recipe for using up very hard or very firm pears and another recipe for your [http://www.guardian.co.uk/lifeandstyle/wordofmouth/2009/may/14/ghent-vegetarian-city-healthy-belgium Gent night]\n\nI have to say that this was one of the best curries I've made in a long while.\n\n'''spice powder'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Grind the following to a powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]:\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[White cumin|white cumin]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[fenugreek seeds]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[Coriander|coriander]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[poppy seeds]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[garam masala]]\n}}\n'''curry'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] or [[ghee]]\n| A big pinch of freshly ground [[black pepper]]\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 5 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 2.5 cm [[Root ginger|root ginger]], peeled and [[Grated|grated]]\n| 1 large [[Red chillies|red chilli]], chopped into rings\n| 450g (1lb) [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] or [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] flesh, peeled and cubed\n| 2 firm [[pears]], peeled, cored and cut into bite-sized chunks\n| 30g mixed dried fruit of your choice\n| 1 tablespoon [[Curry paste|curry paste]]\n| 1 400g can of [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]], rinsed and drained\n| 300 ml [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[jaggery]] or brown sugar \n}}\n'''add during the last 30 minutes of cooking'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 [[kiwi fruit]], peeled and cut into bite-sized chunks\n| 1 [[Banana|banana]], sliced\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\nSet your [[slow cooker]] to medium\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[wok]] or [[frying pan]].  Add the oil or [[ghee]] and a big pinch of [[black pepper]]\n| Gently [[fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] for 4 minutes.  Add the ginger and garlic and fry for a further 2 minutes, stirring so the garlic does not burn\n| Add [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Spices|spices]] and [[Fry|fry]] for a further minute\n| Transfer the spice mix and the remaining ingredients (apart from the last two) into your [[slow cooker]]\n| Mix very well and slow cook for 4 hours\n| Add the [[kiwi fruit]] and sliced [[banana]] 30 minutes before the cooking is completed \n| Add the [[Stock|stock]], bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] until the [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] is soft (about 20 to 40 minutes) \n}}\nIf the [[pears]] are soft then add them for the last 30 minutes so they don't go to mush.\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with homemade [[Naan bread|naan bread]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Abel and Cole veg box recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#slowcooker #pumpkin #fry #blackpepper #pears #kiwifruit #banana #ghee #veryfruitypumpkincurryslowcookerrecipe #simmer #wok </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Za'atar spice mix recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Za'atar spice mix recipe Accompaniments \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#zaatarspicemixrecipe #oliveoil #sumac #zest #meats #oregano #coffeegrinder #hummus #basil #savory #groundmarjoram \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This version of za'atar does not contain sumac. We do have another version that does\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 697\n|PortionCalories = 19\n|DatePublished=20th September 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings =Servings: 36 - Makes 1 small pot - It will keep\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 10 minutes\n|PrepTime = 10 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Za'atar spice mixture.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I like this over lamb cutlets</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis version of [[za'atar]] does not contain [[sumac]].  [[Lebanese za'atar spice mix recipe|We do have another version that does.]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 teaspoons [[basil]]\n| 2 tablespoons  fresh [[ground thyme]]\n| 1 teaspoon dried [[thyme]]\n| 2 teaspoons dried [[oregano]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[savory]]\n| 2 teaspoons  dried [[ground marjoram]]\n| 8 tablespoons [[toasted sesame seeds]]\n| 1 &#189; teaspoons [[sea salt]]\n| [[Zest]] of a [[lemon]], very finely chopped\n| [[Zest]] of a [[lime]], very finely chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Roughly grind the [[sesame seeds]] in a [[mortar and pestle]] or a [[coffee grinder]], set aside\n| Make a finer grind of the remaining ingredients\n| Mix the two together\n| Store in an airtight container, out of the light, for up to 2 months. It begins to lose its flavour if it's stored any longer.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nIt can be used as a seasoning for [[meats]] and [[vegetables]]. \n\nMixed with [[olive oil]] it makes a spread called [[za'atar]]-wu-zayt as a dip for the sesame bread rings known as ka'ak.\n\nYou can spread it on a dough base and bake it as bread, in which case it is called manaeesh bi za'atar. \n\nIt is often eaten as a breakfast snack, sprinkled on labneh (yogurt that has been drained until it becomes a tangy, creamy cheese).\n\nZa'atar is often sprinkled on [[hummus]] or served with [[olive oil]] as a spread or dip.\n\n==See also==\n* [[Lebanese za'atar spice mix recipe]] (with [[sumac]])\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Za'atar]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Za'atar]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces|Za'atar]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Za'atar]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Za'atar]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Za'atar]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#zaatarspicemixrecipe #oliveoil #sumac #zest #meats #oregano #coffeegrinder #hummus #basil #savory #groundmarjoram </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
